<p>The propaganda used by the German <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> in the years leading up to and during <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>'s leadership of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a> (1933–1945) was a crucial instrument for acquiring and maintaining power, and for the implementation of <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi policies</a>. The pervasive use of propaganda by the Nazis is largely responsible for the word "propaganda" itself acquiring its present negative connotations.<sup id="cite_ref-Welch_6_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welch_6-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span id="In_opposition_(1919–33)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="In_opposition_.281919.E2.80.9333.29">In opposition (1919–33)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: In opposition (1919–33)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nazi leader Adolf Hitler devoted three chapters of his 1925/26 book <i><a href="/wiki/Mein_Kampf" title="Mein Kampf">Mein Kampf</a></i>, itself a propaganda tool, to the study and practice of propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> He claimed to have learned the value of propaganda as a <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> infantryman exposed to very effective British and ineffectual German propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The argument that Germany lost the war largely because of <a href="/wiki/British_propaganda_during_World_War_I" title="British propaganda during World War I">British propaganda</a> efforts, expounded at length in <i>Mein Kampf</i>, reflected then-common German nationalist claims. Although untrue – German propaganda during World War I was mostly more advanced than that of the British – it became the official truth of Nazi Germany thanks to its reception by Hitler.<sup id="cite_ref-Welch_11_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welch_11-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Mein Kampf</i> contains the blueprint of later Nazi propaganda efforts. Assessing his audience, Hitler writes in chapter VI:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Propaganda must always address itself to the broad masses of the people. (...) All propaganda must be presented in a popular form and must fix its intellectual level so as not to be above the heads of the least intellectual of those to whom it is directed. (...) The art of propaganda consists precisely in being able to awaken the imagination of the public through an appeal to their feelings, in finding the appropriate psychological form that will arrest the attention and appeal to the hearts of the national masses. The broad masses of the people are not made up of diplomats or professors of public jurisprudence nor simply of persons who are able to form reasoned judgment in given cases, but a vacillating crowd of human children who are constantly wavering between one idea and another. (...) The great majority of a nation is so feminine in its character and outlook that its thought and conduct are ruled by sentiment rather than by sober reasoning. This sentiment, however, is not complex, but simple and consistent. It is not highly differentiated, but has only the negative and positive notions of love and hatred, right and wrong, truth and falsehood."<sup id="cite_ref-MeinKampf_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MeinKampf-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>As to the methods to be employed, he explains:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Propaganda must not investigate the truth objectively and, in so far as it is favourable to the other side, present it according to the theoretical rules of justice; yet it must present only that aspect of the truth which is favourable to its own side. (...) The receptive powers of the masses are very restricted, and their understanding is feeble. On the other hand, they quickly forget. Such being the case, all effective propaganda must be confined to a few bare essentials and those must be expressed as far as possible in stereotyped formulas. These slogans should be persistently repeated until the very last individual has come to grasp the idea that has been put forward. (...) Every change that is made in the subject of a propagandist message must always emphasize the same conclusion. The leading slogan must of course be illustrated in many ways and from several angles, but in the end one must always return to the assertion of the same formula."</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Hitler put these ideas into practice with the reestablishment of the <i><a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lkischer_Beobachter" title="Völkischer Beobachter">Völkischer Beobachter</a></i>, a daily newspaper published by the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> (NSDAP) from February 1925 onwards, whose circulation reached 26,175 in 1929. It was joined in 1927 by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels" title="Joseph Goebbels">Joseph Goebbels</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Angriff" title="Der Angriff">Der Angriff</a></i>, another unabashedly and crudely propagandistic paper.</p>
<p>During most of the Nazis' time in opposition, their means of propaganda remained limited. With little access to mass media, the party continued to rely heavily on Hitler and a few others speaking at public meetings until 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-Welch_13_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welch_13-6">[6]</a></sup> One study finds that the Weimar government's use of pro-government radio propaganda retarded Nazi growth.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-7">[7]</a></sup> In April 1930, Hitler appointed Goebbels head of party propaganda. Goebbels, a former journalist and Nazi party officer in Berlin, soon proved his skills. Among his first successes was the organization of riotous demonstrations that succeeded in having the American anti-war film <i><a href="/wiki/All_Quiet_on_the_Western_Front_(1930_film)" title="All Quiet on the Western Front (1930 film)">All Quiet on the Western Front</a></i> banned in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-Welch_14_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welch_14-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="In_power_(1933–39)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="In_power_.281933.E2.80.9339.29">In power (1933–39)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: In power (1933–39)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolschewismus_ohne_Maske2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/Bolschewismus_ohne_Maske2.jpg/220px-Bolschewismus_ohne_Maske2.jpg" width="220" height="322" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/Bolschewismus_ohne_Maske2.jpg/330px-Bolschewismus_ohne_Maske2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/Bolschewismus_ohne_Maske2.jpg/440px-Bolschewismus_ohne_Maske2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6785" data-file-height="9940" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolschewismus_ohne_Maske2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A 1937 anti-Bolshevik Nazi propaganda poster. The translated caption: "<a href="/wiki/Bolshevism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevism">Bolshevism</a> without a mask – large anti-Bolshevik exhibition of the NSDAP <a href="/wiki/Gauleiter" title="Gauleiter">Gauleitung</a> Berlin from November 6, 1937 to December 19, 1937 in the <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_building" class="mw-redirect" title="Reichstag building">Reichstag building</a>".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 13 March 1933, <a href="/wiki/The_Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="The Third Reich">The Third Reich</a> established a <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Enlightenment_and_Propaganda" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Public Enlightenment and Propaganda">Ministry of Propaganda</a>, appointing Joseph Goebbels as its Minister. Its goals were to establish enemies in the public mind: the external enemies which had imposed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> on Germany, and internal enemies such as <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a>, homosexuals, <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a>, and cultural trends including "<a href="/wiki/Degenerate_art" title="Degenerate art">degenerate art</a>".</p>
<p>A major political and ideological cornerstone of Nazi policy was the unification of all ethnic Germans living outside the Reich's borders (e.g. in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>) under one Greater Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In <i>Mein Kampf</i>, Hitler denounced the pain and misery of ethnic Germans outside Germany, and declared the dream of a common fatherland for which all Germans must fight.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Throughout <i>Mein Kampf</i>, he pushed Germans worldwide to make the struggle for political power and independence their main focus, made official in the <i><a href="/wiki/Heim_ins_Reich" title="Heim ins Reich">Heim ins Reich</a></i> policy beginning in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>For months prior to the beginning of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in 1939, German newspapers and leaders had carried out a national and international propaganda campaign accusing Polish authorities of organizing or tolerating violent <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> of <a href="/wiki/German_minority_in_Poland" title="German minority in Poland">ethnic Germans</a> living in Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-German_Editor_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-German_Editor-12">[12]</a></sup> On 22 August, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> told his generals:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"I will provide a propagandistic <i><a href="/wiki/Casus_belli" title="Casus belli">casus belli</a></i>. Its credibility doesn't matter. The victor will not be asked whether he told the truth."<sup id="cite_ref-WirtzGordon_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WirtzGordon-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lightbody_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lightbody-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The main part of this propaganda campaign was the <a href="/wiki/False_flag" title="False flag">false flag</a> <a href="/wiki/Operation_Himmler" title="Operation Himmler">Operation Himmler</a>, which was designed to create the appearance of <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Polish</a> aggression against Germany, in order to justify the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland_(1939)" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Poland (1939)">invasion of Poland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WirtzGordon_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WirtzGordon-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lightbody_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lightbody-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Himmler_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Himmler-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Research finds that the Nazis' use of radio propaganda helped it consolidate power and enroll more party members.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-semitism">Anti-semitism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Anti-semitism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EwigerJudeFilm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/86/EwigerJudeFilm.jpg/200px-EwigerJudeFilm.jpg" width="200" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/86/EwigerJudeFilm.jpg/300px-EwigerJudeFilm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/86/EwigerJudeFilm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="451" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EwigerJudeFilm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Poster for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Eternal_Jew_(1940_film)" title="The Eternal Jew (1940 film)">The Eternal Jew</a></i> directed by Fritz Hippler</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Adolf Hitler and Nazi propagandists played on widespread and long-established German <a href="/wiki/Anti-Semitism" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Semitism">anti-Semitism</a>. The Jews were blamed for things such as robbing the German people of their hard work while themselves avoiding physical labour. Hitler declared that the mission of the Nazi movement was to annihilate "<a href="/wiki/Jewish_Bolshevism" title="Jewish Bolshevism">Jewish Bolshevism</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Hitler asserted that the "three vices" of "Jewish Marxism" were democracy, pacifism and internationalism,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and that the Jews were behind Bolshevism, communism and Marxism.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Joseph Goebbels in the 1937 The Great Anti-Bolshevist Exhibition declared that Bolshevism and Jewry were the same thing.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the 1935 Nazi party congress rally at Nuremberg, Goebbels declared that "Bolshevism is the declaration of war by Jewish-led international subhumans against culture itself."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Der_St%C3%BCrmer" title="Der Stürmer">Der Stürmer</a></i>, a Nazi propaganda newspaper, told Germans that Jews kidnapped small children before <a href="/wiki/Passover" title="Passover">Passover</a> because <a href="/wiki/Blood_libel" title="Blood libel">"Jews need the blood of a Christian child, maybe, to mix in with their Matzah."</a> Posters, films, cartoons, and fliers were seen throughout Germany which attacked the Jewish community. One of the most infamous such films was <a href="/wiki/The_Eternal_Jew_(1940_film)" title="The Eternal Jew (1940 film)">The Eternal Jew</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Hippler" title="Fritz Hippler">Fritz Hippler</a>.</p>
<p>A study finds that the Nazis' use of radio propaganda incited anti-Semitic acts. Nazi radio was most effective in places where anti-Semitism was historically high but had a negative effect in places with historically low anti-Semitism.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Euthanasia">Euthanasia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Euthanasia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Racial_hygiene" title="Racial hygiene">Racial hygiene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_eugenics" title="Nazi eugenics">Nazi eugenics</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Law_for_the_Prevention_of_Hereditarily_Diseased_Offspring" title="Law for the Prevention of Hereditarily Diseased Offspring">Law for the Prevention of Hereditarily Diseased Offspring</a> was introduced on 14 July 1933, and various propaganda was used to target the disabled.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> A special <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a> program, called <a href="/wiki/T-4_Euthanasia_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="T-4 Euthanasia Program">T-4 Euthanasia Program</a> began in 1939, related propaganda arguments were based on the books, <i>Die Freigabe der Vernichtung lebensunwerten Lebens</i> ("Allowing the Destruction of <a href="/wiki/Life_Unworthy_of_Living" class="mw-redirect" title="Life Unworthy of Living">Life Unworthy of Living</a>"), written by <a href="/wiki/Karl_Binding" title="Karl Binding">Karl Binding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Hoche" title="Alfred Hoche">Alfred Hoche</a> and the book <i>Human Heredity Theory and Racial Hygiene</i>, written by <a href="/wiki/Eugen_Fischer" title="Eugen Fischer">Eugen Fischer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Baur" title="Erwin Baur">Erwin Baur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Lenz" title="Fritz Lenz">Fritz Lenz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuremberg_Laws">Nuremberg Laws</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nuremberg Laws">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1935, anti-semitic laws in Nazi Germany were introduced known as the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>, the laws forbid non-Aryans and political opponents of the Nazis from the civil-service and any sexual relations and marriage between people classified as "Aryan" and "non-Aryan" (Jews, Gypsies, blacks) was prohibited as <i><a href="/wiki/Rassenschande" title="Rassenschande">Rassenschande</a></i> or "race defilement".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The Nuremberg Laws were based on notions of racial purity and sought to preserve the Aryan race, who were at the top of the Nazi racial hierarchy and were said to be the ubermenschen "herrenvolk" (master race),<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and to teach the German nation to view the Jews as subhumans.<sup id="cite_ref-Arad1999_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arad1999-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_opponents">Political opponents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Political opponents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Soon after the takeover of power in 1933, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a> were established for political opponents. The first people that were sent to the camps were Communists.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> They were sent because of their ties with the Soviet Union and because Nazism greatly opposed Communism.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Nazi propaganda dismissed the Communists as "Red subhumans".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Goebbels used the death of Horst Wessel who was killed in 1930 by two members of the Communist Party of Germany as a propaganda tool for the Nazis against "Communist subhumans".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Treaty_of_Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Treaty of Versailles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> was signed in 1919, non-propagandists newspapers headlines across the nation spoke German's feelings, such as <i>"schändlich!"</i>("Unacceptable!") which appeared on the front page of the <i>Frankfurter Zeitung</i> in 1919. The <i>Berliner Tageblatt</i>, also in 1919, predicted "Should we accept the conditions, a military furore for revenge will sound in Germany within a few years, a militant nationalism will engulf all."<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Hitler, knowing his nation's disgust with the Treaty, used it as leverage to influence his audience. He would repeatedly refer back to the terms of the Treaty as a direct attack on Germany and its people. In one speech delivered on 30 January 1937 he directly stated that he was withdrawing the German signature from the document to protest the outrageous proportions of the terms. He claimed the Treaty made Germany out to be inferior and "less" of a country than others only because blame for the war was placed on it. The success of Nazi propagandists and Hitler won the Nazi party control of Germany and eventually led to World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="At_war_(1939–45)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="At_war_.281939.E2.80.9345.29">At war (1939–45)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: At war (1939–45)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27915,_Danzig,_Enfernen_eines_polnischen_Hoheitszeichens.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27915%2C_Danzig%2C_Enfernen_eines_polnischen_Hoheitszeichens.jpg/150px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27915%2C_Danzig%2C_Enfernen_eines_polnischen_Hoheitszeichens.jpg" width="150" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27915%2C_Danzig%2C_Enfernen_eines_polnischen_Hoheitszeichens.jpg/225px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27915%2C_Danzig%2C_Enfernen_eines_polnischen_Hoheitszeichens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27915%2C_Danzig%2C_Enfernen_eines_polnischen_Hoheitszeichens.jpg/300px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27915%2C_Danzig%2C_Enfernen_eines_polnischen_Hoheitszeichens.jpg 2x" data-file-width="510" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-H27915,_Danzig,_Enfernen_eines_polnischen_Hoheitszeichens.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> soldiers dismantling Polish government insignia in <a href="/wiki/Gdingen" class="mw-redirect" title="Gdingen">Gdingen</a> soon after the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">invasion of Poland</a> in 1939.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nur_fur_deutsche.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Nur_fur_deutsche.jpg/160px-Nur_fur_deutsche.jpg" width="160" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Nur_fur_deutsche.jpg/240px-Nur_fur_deutsche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Nur_fur_deutsche.jpg/320px-Nur_fur_deutsche.jpg 2x" data-file-width="544" data-file-height="760" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nur_fur_deutsche.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nur_f%C3%BCr_deutsche_Fahrg%C3%A4ste&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nur für deutsche Fahrgäste (page does not exist)">Nur für deutsche Fahrgäste</a> ("Only for German Passengers")</i>, a Nazi slogan used in occupied territories, mainly posted at entrances to parks, cafes, cinemas, theatres and other facilities.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Until the conclusion of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a> on 2 February 1943, German propaganda emphasized the prowess of German arms and the humanity German soldiers had shown to the peoples of occupied territories. Pilots of the Allied bombing fleets were depicted as cowardly murderers, and Americans in particular as gangsters in the style of <a href="/wiki/Al_Capone" title="Al Capone">Al Capone</a>. At the same time, German propaganda sought to alienate Americans and British from each other, and both these Western nations from the Soviet Union. One of the primary sources for propaganda was the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmachtbericht" title="Wehrmachtbericht">Wehrmachtbericht</a>, a daily radio broadcast from the High Command of the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a>, the <a href="/wiki/OKW" class="mw-redirect" title="OKW">OKW</a>. Nazi victories lent themselves easily to propaganda broadcasts and were at this point difficult to mishandle.<sup id="cite_ref-Michael_Balfour_p234_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Michael_Balfour_p234-32">[32]</a></sup> Satires on the defeated, accounts of attacks, and praise for the fallen all were useful for Nazis.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Still, failures were not easily handled even at this stage. For example, considerable embarrassment resulted when the <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ark_Royal_(91)#Another_near_miss" title="HMS Ark Royal (91)"><i>Ark Royal</i></a> proved to have survived an attack that German propaganda had hyped.<sup id="cite_ref-Michael_Balfour_p234_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Michael_Balfour_p234-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Stalingrad, the main theme changed to Germany as the sole defender of what they called "Western European culture" against the "Bolshevist hordes". The introduction of the <a href="/wiki/V-1_(flying_bomb)" class="mw-redirect" title="V-1 (flying bomb)">V-1</a> and <a href="/wiki/V-2" class="mw-redirect" title="V-2">V-2</a> "vengeance weapons" was emphasized to convince Britons of the hopelessness of defeating Germany.</p>
<p>Problems in propaganda arose easily in this stage; expectations of success were raised too high and too quickly, which required explanation if they were not fulfilled, and blunted the effects of success, and the hushing of blunders and failures caused mistrust.<sup id="cite_ref-Michael_Balfour_p234_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Michael_Balfour_p234-32">[32]</a></sup> The increasing hardship of the war for the German people also called forth more propaganda that the war had been forced on the German people by the refusal of foreign powers to accept their strength and independence.<sup id="cite_ref-Michael_Balfour_p234_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Michael_Balfour_p234-32">[32]</a></sup> Goebbels called for propaganda to toughen up the German people and not make victory look easy.<sup id="cite_ref-Michael_Balfour_p234_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Michael_Balfour_p234-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 June 1944, the Nazis permitted the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> to visit the <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp_Theresienstadt" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp Theresienstadt">concentration camp Theresienstadt</a> to dispel rumors about the <a href="/wiki/Final_Solution" title="Final Solution">Final Solution</a>, which was intended to kill all Jews. In reality, Theresienstadt was a transit camp for Jews en route to <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a>. In a sophisticated propaganda effort, fake shops and cafés were erected to imply that the Jews lived in relative comfort. The guests enjoyed the performance of a children's opera, <i><a href="/wiki/Brundibar" class="mw-redirect" title="Brundibar">Brundibar</a></i>, written by inmate <a href="/wiki/Hans_Kr%C3%A1sa" title="Hans Krása">Hans Krása</a>. The hoax was so successful for the Nazis that they went on to make a propaganda film <i><a href="/wiki/Theresienstadt_(film)" title="Theresienstadt (film)">Theresienstadt</a></i>. Shooting of the film began on 26 February 1944. Directed by <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Gerron" title="Kurt Gerron">Kurt Gerron</a>, it was meant to show how well the Jews lived under the "benevolent" protection of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a>. After the shooting, most of the cast, and even the filmmaker himself, were deported to the concentration camp of <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Auschwitz">Auschwitz</a> where they were murdered. <a href="/wiki/Hans_Fritzsche" title="Hans Fritzsche">Hans Fritzsche</a>, who had been head of the Radio Chamber, was tried and acquitted by the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Trials" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg Trials">Nuremberg war crimes tribunal</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-semitism_during_World_War_II">Anti-semitism during World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Anti-semitism during World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Anti-semitic wartime propaganda served a variety of purposes. It was hoped that people in Allied countries would be persuaded that Jews should be blamed for the war. The Nazis also wished to ensure that German people were aware of the extreme measures being carried out against the Jews on their behalf, in order to incriminate them and thus guarantee their continued loyalty through fear by Nazi-conjectured scenarios of supposed post-war "Jewish" reprisals.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Especially from 1942 onwards,</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>the announcement that Jews were being exterminated served as a group unification factor to preclude desertion and force the Germans to continue fighting. Germans were fed the knowledge that too many atrocities had been committed, especially against the Jews, to allow for an understanding to be reached with the Allies.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— David Bankier (2002) <i>The Use of Antisemitism in Nazi Wartime Propaganda</i><sup id="cite_ref-Berenbaum2002_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berenbaum2002-36">[36]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Books">Books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Nazis and sympathizers published many books. Most of the beliefs that would become associated with the Nazis, such as German nationalism, <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">eugenics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anti-Semitism" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Semitism">anti-Semitism</a> had been in circulation since the 19th century, and the Nazis seized on this body of existing work in their own publications.</p>
<p>The most notable is <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Mein_Kampf" title="Mein Kampf">Mein Kampf</a></i> detailing his beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The book outlines major ideas that would later culminate in World War II. It is heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Le_Bon" title="Gustave Le Bon">Gustave Le Bon</a>'s 1895 <i>The Crowd: A Study of the Popular Mind</i>, which theorized propaganda as a way to control the seemingly irrational behaviour of crowds. Particularly prominent is the violent anti-Semitism of Hitler and his associates, drawing, among other sources, on the fabricated "<a href="/wiki/Protocols_of_the_Elders_of_Zion" class="mw-redirect" title="Protocols of the Elders of Zion">Protocols of the Elders of Zion</a>" (1897), which implied that Jews secretly conspired to rule the world. This book was a key source of propaganda for the Nazis and helped fuel their common hatred against the Jews during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-McKale_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKale-38">[38]</a></sup> For example, Hitler claimed that the international language <a href="/wiki/Esperanto" title="Esperanto">Esperanto</a> was part of a Jewish plot and makes arguments toward the old German nationalist ideas of "<a href="/wiki/Drang_nach_Osten" title="Drang nach Osten">Drang nach Osten</a>" and the necessity to gain <a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a> ("living space") eastwards (especially in Russia). Other books such as <i>Rassenkunde des deutschen Volkes</i> (Ethnology of German People) by <a href="/wiki/Hans_F._K._G%C3%BCnther" title="Hans F. K. Günther">Hans F. K. Günther</a> and <i>Rasse und Seele</i> (Race and Soul) by Dr. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ludwig_Ferdinand_Clauss&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ludwig Ferdinand Clauss (page does not exist)">Ludwig Ferdinand Clauss</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ludwig_Ferdinand_Clauss" class="extiw" title="de:Ludwig Ferdinand Clauss">de</a>)</span> attempt to identify and classify the differences between the German, <a href="/wiki/Nordic_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordic theory">Nordic</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Aryan</a> type and other supposedly inferior peoples. These books were used as texts in German schools during the Nazi era.</p>
<p>The pre-existing and popular genre of <i>Schollen-roman</i>, or novel of the soil, also known as <i><a href="/wiki/Blood_and_soil" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood and soil">blood and soil</a></i> novels,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> was given a boost by the acceptability of its themes to the Nazis and developed a mysticism of unity.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The immensely popular "Red Indian" stories by <a href="/wiki/Karl_May" title="Karl May">Karl May</a> were permitted despite the heroic treatment of the hero <a href="/wiki/Winnetou" title="Winnetou">Winnetou</a> and "colored" races; instead, the argument was made that the stories demonstrated the fall of the Red Indians was caused by a lack of racial consciousness, to encourage it in the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-Lynn_H_p._79_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lynn_H_p._79-41">[41]</a></sup> Other fictional works were also adapted; <i><a href="/wiki/Heidi" title="Heidi">Heidi</a></i> was stripped of its Christian elements, and <a href="/wiki/Robinson_Crusoe" title="Robinson Crusoe">Robinson Crusoe</a>'s relationship to Friday was made a master-slave one.<sup id="cite_ref-Claudia_Koonz_p_143_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Claudia_Koonz_p_143-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Children's books also made their appearance. In 1938, <a href="/wiki/Julius_Streicher" title="Julius Streicher">Julius Streicher</a> published <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Giftpilz" title="Der Giftpilz">Der Giftpilz</a></i> (The Poisonous Mushroom), a storybook that equated the Jewish people to poisonous mushrooms and aimed to educate children about the Jews. The book was an example of <a href="/wiki/Anti-Semitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Semitic">anti-Semitic</a> propaganda and stated that, "The following tales tell the truth about the Jewish poison mushroom. They show the many shapes the Jew assumes. They show the depravity and baseness of the Jewish race. They show the Jew for what he really is: The Devil in human form."<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Textbooks">Textbooks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Textbooks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>"Geopolitical atlases" emphasized Nazi schemes, demonstrating the "encirclement" of Germany, depicting how the prolific Slav nations would cause the German people to be overrun, and (in contrast) showing <a href="/wiki/Volk_ohne_Raum" title="Volk ohne Raum">the relative population density of Germany</a> was much higher than that of the Eastern regions (where they would seek <a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._76_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._76-44">[44]</a></sup> Textbooks would often show that the birth rate amongst Slavs was prolific compared to Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Geography text books stated how crowded Germany had become.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Other charts would show the cost of disabled children as opposed to healthy ones, or show how two-child families threatened the birthrate.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Math books discussed military applications and used military word problems, physics and chemistry concentrated on military applications, and grammar classes were devoted to propaganda sentences.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Other textbooks dealt with the history of the Nazi Party.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Elementary school reading text included large amounts of propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Children were taught through textbooks that they were the Aryan <a href="/wiki/Master_race" title="Master race">master race</a> (<i>Herrenvolk</i>) while the Jews were untrustworthy, parasitic and <i><a href="/wiki/Untermenschen" class="mw-redirect" title="Untermenschen">Untermenschen</a></i> (inferior subhumans).<sup id="cite_ref-Pine2010_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pine2010-51">[51]</a></sup> Course content and textbooks unnecessarily included information that was propagandistic, an attempt to sway the children's views from an early age.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maps showing the racial composition of Europe were banned from the classroom after many efforts that did not define the territory widely enough for party officials.<sup id="cite_ref-overy260_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overy260-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Even <a href="/wiki/Fairy_tale" title="Fairy tale">fairy tales</a> were put to use, with <i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella" title="Cinderella">Cinderella</a></i> being presented as a tale of how the prince's racial instincts lead him to reject the stepmother's alien blood (present in her daughters) for the racially pure maiden.<sup id="cite_ref-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._77-8_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._77-8-54">[54]</a></sup> Nordic sagas were likewise presented as the illustration of <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrerprinzip" title="Führerprinzip">Führerprinzip</a>, which was developed with such heroes as <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> and <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._78_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._78-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Literature was to be chosen within the "German spirit" rather than a fixed list of forbidden and required, which made the teachers all the more cautious<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> although Jewish authors were impossible for classrooms.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> While only <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Macbeth" title="Macbeth">Macbeth</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Merchant_of_Venice" title="The Merchant of Venice">The Merchant of Venice</a></i> were actually recommended, none of the plays were actually forbidden, even <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet" title="Hamlet">Hamlet</a></i>, denounced for "flabbiness of soul."<sup id="cite_ref-Milton_Mayer_p193_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milton_Mayer_p193-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Biology texts, however, were put to the most use in presenting eugenic principles and racial theories; this included explanations of the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>, which were claimed to allow the German and Jewish peoples to co-exist without the danger of mixing.<sup id="cite_ref-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._85_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._85-59">[59]</a></sup> Science was to be presented as the most natural area for introducing the "Jewish Question" once teachers took care to point out that in nature, animals associated with those of their own species.<sup id="cite_ref-questionineducation_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-questionineducation-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Teachers' guidelines on racial instruction presented both the handicapped and Jews as dangers.<sup id="cite_ref-guidelines_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guidelines-61">[61]</a></sup> Despite their many photographs glamorising the "Nordic" type, the texts also claimed that visual inspection was insufficient, and genealogical analysis was required to determine their types and report any hereditary problems.<sup id="cite_ref-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._86_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lynn_H._Nicholas_p._86-62">[62]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Teachers_League" title="National Socialist Teachers League">National Socialist Teachers League</a> (NSLB) stressed that at primary schools, in particular, they had to work on only the Nordic racial core of the German <i>Volk</i> again and again and contrast it with the racial composition of foreign populations and the Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-Pine2010_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pine2010-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Books_for_occupied_countries">Books for occupied countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Books for occupied countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In occupied France, the German Institute encouraged translation of German works although chiefly German nationalists, not ardent Nazis, produced a massive increase in the sale of translated works.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The only books in English to be sold were English classics, and books with Jewish authors or Jewish subject matter (such as biographies) were banned, except for some scientific works.<sup id="cite_ref-nuremberg51_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuremberg51-64">[64]</a></sup> Control of the paper supply allowed Germans the easy ability to pressure publishers about books.<sup id="cite_ref-nuremberg51_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuremberg51-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comics">Comics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Comics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Nazi-controlled government in German-occupied France produced the <i>Vica</i> comic book series during World War II as a propaganda tool against the Allied forces. The Vica series, authored by Vincent Krassousky, represented Nazi influence and perspective in French society, and included such titles as <i>Vica contre le service secret anglais</i>, and <i>Vica défie l'Oncle Sam</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Films">Films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Nazism_and_cinema" title="Nazism and cinema">Nazism and cinema</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_films_1933-1945" class="mw-redirect" title="List of German films 1933-1945">List of German films 1933-1945</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_152-42-31,_N%C3%BCrnberg,_Leni_Riefenstahl_mit_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Bundesarchiv_Bild_152-42-31%2C_N%C3%BCrnberg%2C_Leni_Riefenstahl_mit_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_152-42-31%2C_N%C3%BCrnberg%2C_Leni_Riefenstahl_mit_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Bundesarchiv_Bild_152-42-31%2C_N%C3%BCrnberg%2C_Leni_Riefenstahl_mit_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_152-42-31%2C_N%C3%BCrnberg%2C_Leni_Riefenstahl_mit_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Bundesarchiv_Bild_152-42-31%2C_N%C3%BCrnberg%2C_Leni_Riefenstahl_mit_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_152-42-31%2C_N%C3%BCrnberg%2C_Leni_Riefenstahl_mit_Heinrich_Himmler.jpg 2x" data-file-width="727" data-file-height="458" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbcaption">

The <i>Totenehrung</i> (honouring of dead) at the 1934 <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Rally" title="Nuremberg Rally">Nuremberg Rally</a>. <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">SA</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Lutze" title="Viktor Lutze">Viktor Lutze</a> (from L to R) on the stone terrace in front of the <i>Ehrenhalle</i> (Hall of Honour) in the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_party_rally_grounds#Luitpoldarena" title="Nazi party rally grounds">Luitpoldarena</a>. In the background is the crescent-shaped <i>Ehrentribüne</i> (literally: tribune of honour).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Nazis produced many films to promote their views, using the party's <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Film_(Nazi_Germany)" title="Department of Film (Nazi Germany)">Department of Film</a> for organizing film propaganda. An estimated 45 million people attended film screenings put on by the NSDAP.<sup id="cite_ref-calvin.edu_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-calvin.edu-66">[66]</a></sup> Reichsamtsleiter Neumann declared that the goal of the Department of Film was not directly political in nature, but was rather to influence the culture, education, and entertainment of the general population.<sup id="cite_ref-calvin.edu_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-calvin.edu-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 September 1933, a <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Film" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Film">Department of Film</a> was incorporated into the Chamber of Culture. The department controlled the licensing of every film prior to its production. Sometimes the government selected the actors for a film, financed the production partially or totally, and granted tax breaks to the producers. Awards for "valuable" films would decrease taxes, thus encouraging self-censorship among movie makers.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Under Goebbels and Hitler, the <a href="/wiki/German_film_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="German film industry">German film industry</a> became entirely nationalised. The National Socialist Propaganda Directorate, which Goebbels oversaw, had at its disposal nearly all film agencies in Germany by 1936. Occasionally, certain directors such as <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Liebeneiner" title="Wolfgang Liebeneiner">Wolfgang Liebeneiner</a> were able to bypass Goebbels by providing him with a different version of the film than would be released. Such films include those directed by <a href="/wiki/Helmut_K%C3%A4utner" title="Helmut Käutner">Helmut Käutner</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Romance_in_a_Minor_Key" title="Romance in a Minor Key">Romanze in Moll</a></i> (<i>Romance in a Minor Key</i>, 1943), <i><a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9Fe_Freiheit_Nr._7" title="Große Freiheit Nr. 7">Große Freiheit Nr. 7</a></i> (<i>The Great Freedom, No. 7</i>, 1944), and <i><a href="/wiki/Under_the_Bridges" title="Under the Bridges">Unter den Brücken</a></i> (<i>Under the Bridges</i>, 1945).</p>
<p>Schools were also provided with motion picture projectors because film was regarded as particularly appropriate for propagandizing children.<sup id="cite_ref-rhodes21_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rhodes21-68">[68]</a></sup> Films specifically created for schools were termed "military education."<sup id="cite_ref-rhodes21_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rhodes21-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Triumph_des_Willens" class="mw-redirect" title="Triumph des Willens">Triumph des Willens</a></i> (<i>Triumph of the Will</i>, 1935) by film-maker <a href="/wiki/Leni_Riefenstahl" title="Leni Riefenstahl">Leni Riefenstahl</a> chronicled the Nazi Party Congress of 1934 in <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>. It followed an earlier film of the 1933 <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Rally" title="Nuremberg Rally">Nuremberg Rally</a> produced by Riefenstahl, <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Sieg_des_Glaubens" class="mw-redirect" title="Der Sieg des Glaubens">Der Sieg des Glaubens</a></i>. <i>Triumph of the Will</i> features footage of uniformed party members (though relatively few German soldiers), who are marching and drilling to <a href="/wiki/Militaristic" class="mw-redirect" title="Militaristic">militaristic</a> tunes. The film contains excerpts from speeches given by various <a href="/wiki/Nazi_leaders" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi leaders">Nazi leaders</a> at the Congress, including <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. <a href="/wiki/Frank_Capra" title="Frank Capra">Frank Capra</a> used scenes from the film, which he described partially as "the ominous prelude of Hitler's holocaust of hate", in many parts of the United States government's <i><a href="/wiki/Why_We_Fight" title="Why We Fight">Why We Fight</a></i> anti-Axis seven film series, to demonstrate what the personnel of the American military would be facing in World War II, and why the Axis had to be defeated.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Eternal_Jew_(1940_film)" title="The Eternal Jew (1940 film)">Der ewige Jude</a></i> (<i>The Eternal Jew</i>, 1940) was directed by <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Hippler" title="Fritz Hippler">Fritz Hippler</a> at the insistence of Goebbels, though the writing is credited to <a href="/wiki/Eberhard_Taubert" title="Eberhard Taubert">Eberhard Taubert</a>. The movie is done in the style of a documentary, the central thesis being the immutable racial personality traits that characterize the Jew as a wandering cultural parasite. Throughout the film, these traits are contrasted to the Nazi state ideal: while Aryan men find satisfaction in physical labour and the creation of value, Jews only find pleasure in money and a hedonist lifestyle.</p>
<p>A main medium was <a href="/wiki/Die_Deutsche_Wochenschau" title="Die Deutsche Wochenschau">Die Deutsche Wochenschau</a>, a newsreel series produced for cinemas, from 1940. Newsreels were explicitly intended to portray German interests as successful.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Themes often included the virtues of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordic theory">Nordic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Aryan" title="Aryan">Aryan</a> type, German military and industrial strength, and the evils of the Nazi enemies.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_art">Fine art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fine art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ArnoBrekerDiePartei.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/ArnoBrekerDiePartei.jpg/220px-ArnoBrekerDiePartei.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/ArnoBrekerDiePartei.jpg/330px-ArnoBrekerDiePartei.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/ArnoBrekerDiePartei.jpg/440px-ArnoBrekerDiePartei.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1747" data-file-height="1183" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ArnoBrekerDiePartei.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Arno_Breker" title="Arno Breker">Arno Breker</a>'s sculptures of the Nordic man made him Hitler's favorite sculptor.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nazi_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi art">Nazi art</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Degenerate_art" title="Degenerate art">Degenerate art</a></div>
<p>By Nazi standards, fine art was not propaganda. Its purpose was to create ideals, for eternity.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> This produced a call for heroic and romantic art, which reflected the ideal rather than the realistic.<sup id="cite_ref-overy260_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overy260-53">[53]</a></sup> Explicitly political paintings were very rare.<sup id="cite_ref-Frederic_Spotts_p_176_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frederic_Spotts_p_176-72">[72]</a></sup> Still more rare were anti-Semitic paintings, because the art was supposed to be on a higher plane.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Nevertheless, selected themes, common in propaganda, were the most common topics of art.</p>
<p>Sculpture was used as an expression of Nazi racial theories.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The most common image was of the nude male, expressing the ideal of the Aryan race.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Nudes were required to be physically perfect.<sup id="cite_ref-sontag3_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sontag3-76">[76]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Exposition_of_1937" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Exposition of 1937">Paris Exposition of 1937</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josef_Thorak" title="Josef Thorak">Josef Thorak</a>'s <i>Comradeship</i> stood outside the German pavilion, depicting two enormous nude males, clasping hands and standing defiantly side by side, in a pose of defense and racial camaraderie.<sup id="cite_ref-overy260_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overy260-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Landscape_painting" title="Landscape painting">Landscape painting</a> featured mostly heavily in the Greater German Art exhibition,<sup id="cite_ref-Frederic_Spotts_p_176_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frederic_Spotts_p_176-72">[72]</a></sup> in accordance with themes of <a href="/wiki/Blood_and_soil" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood and soil">blood and soil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Peasants were also popular images, reflecting a simple life in harmony with nature,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> frequently with large families.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> With the advent of war, war art came to be a significant though still not predominating proportion.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The continuing of the German Art Exhibition throughout the war was put forth as a manifestation of German's culture.<sup id="cite_ref-immortal_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immortal-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Magazines">Magazines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Magazines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In and after 1939, the <i>Zeitschriften-Dienst</i> was sent to magazines to provide guidelines on what to write for appropriate topics.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Nazi publications also carried various forms of propaganda.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Neues_Volk" title="Neues Volk">Neues Volk</a></i> was a monthly publication of the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Racial_Policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of Racial Policy">Office of Racial Policy</a>, which answered questions about acceptable race relations.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> While mainly focused on race relations, it also included articles about the strength and character of the Aryan race compared to Jews and other "defectives".<sup id="cite_ref-Claudia_Koonz_p_119_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Claudia_Koonz_p_119-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/NS-Frauen-Warte" title="NS-Frauen-Warte">NS-Frauen-Warte</a></i>, aimed at women, included such topics as the role of women in the Nazi state.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Despite its propaganda elements, it was predominantly a woman's magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-rupp45_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rupp45-86">[86]</a></sup> It defended <a href="/wiki/Anti-intellectualism" title="Anti-intellectualism">anti-intellectualism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Spirit_of_Race_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Spirit_of_Race-87">[87]</a></sup> urged women to have children, even in wartime,<sup id="cite_ref-Ready_to_Die_Ready_to_Live_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ready_to_Die_Ready_to_Live-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Life_Must_Win_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life_Must_Win-89">[89]</a></sup> put forth what the Nazis had done for women,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> discussed bridal schools,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> and urged women to greater efforts in <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">total war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Strength_from_Love_and_Faith_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strength_from_Love_and_Faith-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Der_Pimpf" title="Der Pimpf">Der Pimpf</a></i> was aimed at boys, and contained both adventure and propaganda.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Das_deutsche_M%C3%A4del" class="mw-redirect" title="Das deutsche Mädel">Das deutsche Mädel</a></i>, in contrast, recommended that girls take up hiking, tending the wounded, and preparing to care for children.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Far more than <i>NS-Frauen-Warte</i>, it emphasized the strong and active German woman.<sup id="cite_ref-rupp45_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rupp45-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Signal">Signal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Signal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Signal_(magazine)" title="Signal (magazine)">Signal (magazine)</a></div>
<p><i>Signal</i> was a propaganda magazine published by the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> and distributed throughout <a href="/wiki/Occupied_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupied Europe">occupied Europe</a> and neutral countries. Published from April 1940 to March 1945, "Signal" had the highest sales of any magazine published in Europe during the period—circulation peaked at 2.5&#160;million in 1943. At various times, it was published in at least twenty languages. An English edition was distributed in the British <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands#20th_century" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alderney" title="Alderney">Alderney</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sark" title="Sark">Sark</a>, which were <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Channel_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of the Channel Islands">occupied by the Wehrmacht</a> during the war.</p>
<p>The promoter of the magazine was the chief of the Wehrmacht propaganda office, Colonel Hasso von Wedel. Its annual budget was 10 million Reichmarks, roughly $2.5&#160;million at the pre-war exchange rate.</p>
<p>The image that <i>Signal</i> transmitted was that of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and its <a href="/wiki/New_Order_(political_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="New Order (political system)">New Order</a> as the great benefactor of European peoples and of <a href="/wiki/Western_civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Western civilization">Western civilization</a> in general. The danger of a Soviet invasion of Europe was strongly pointed out. The quality of the magazine itself was quite high, featuring complete reviews from the front lines rich in information and photos, even displaying a double center-page full-colour picture. In fact, many of the most famous <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> photos that are to be seen today come from <i>Signal</i>. The magazine contained little to no <a href="/wiki/Anti-Semitism" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Semitism">anti-Semitic</a> propaganda, as the contents were mainly military.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DasSchwarzeKorps1937.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/DasSchwarzeKorps1937.jpg/220px-DasSchwarzeKorps1937.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/DasSchwarzeKorps1937.jpg/330px-DasSchwarzeKorps1937.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/25/DasSchwarzeKorps1937.jpg 2x" data-file-width="375" data-file-height="565" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DasSchwarzeKorps1937.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Das Schwarze Korps</i> (<i>The Black Corps</i>), the official <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a> newspaper.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lkischer_Beobachter" title="Völkischer Beobachter">Völkischer Beobachter</a></i> ("People's Observer") was the official daily newspaper of the NSDAP since December 1920. It disseminated Nazi ideology in the form of brief hyperboles directed against the weakness of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentarism" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentarism">parliamentarism</a>, the evils of Jewry and Bolshevism, the national humiliation of the <a href="/wiki/Versailles_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Versailles Treaty">Versailles Treaty</a> and other such topics.<sup id="cite_ref-Welch_12_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welch_12-99">[99]</a></sup> It was joined in 1926 by <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Angriff" title="Der Angriff">Der Angriff</a></i> ("The Attack"), a weekly and later daily paper founded by Joseph Goebbels. It was mainly dedicated to attacks against political opponents and Jews – one of its most striking features were vehemently antisemitic cartoons by <a href="/wiki/Hans_Schweitzer" title="Hans Schweitzer">Hans Schweitzer</a> – but also engaged in the glorification of Nazi heroes such as <a href="/wiki/Horst_Wessel" title="Horst Wessel">Horst Wessel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Welch_13_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welch_13-6">[6]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Illustrierter_Beobachter" title="Illustrierter Beobachter">Illustrierter Beobachter</a></i> was their weekly illustrated paper.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other Nazi publications included</p>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Das_Reich_(newspaper)" title="Das Reich (newspaper)">Das Reich</a></i>, a more moderate and highbrow publication aimed at intellectuals and foreigners;</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Der_St%C3%BCrmer" title="Der Stürmer">Der Stürmer</a></i>, the most virulently antisemitic of all;<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> and</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Das_Schwarze_Korps" title="Das Schwarze Korps">Das Schwarze Korps</a></i>, an <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a> publication, aiming at a more intellectual tone.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>After Hitler's rise to power in 1933, all of the regular press came under complete Nazi editorial control through the policy of <i><a href="/wiki/Gleichschaltung" title="Gleichschaltung">Gleichschaltung</a></i>, and short-lived propaganda newspapers were also established in the conquered territories during World War II. Alfred Rosenberg was a key member of the Nazi party who gained control of their newspaper which was openly praised by Hitler. However, Hitler was dissatisfied by Rosenberg's work and slandered Rosenberg behind his back, discrediting his work.<sup id="cite_ref-Herzstein_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herzstein-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers_in_occupied_countries">Newspapers in occupied countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Newspapers in occupied countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Ukraine, after Nazis cracked down on the papers, most papers printed only articles from German agencies, producing the odd effect of more anti-American and anti-British articles than anti-Communist ones.<sup id="cite_ref-harvest192_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harvest192-104">[104]</a></sup> They also printed articles about antecedents of German rule over Ukraine, such as <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-harvest192_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harvest192-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Photography">Photography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Photography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460,_Adolf_Hitler,_Rednerposen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="624" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460,_Adolf_Hitler,_Rednerposen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Adolf Hitler rehearsing poses for his speeches in photos reportedly taken in 1927.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Nazis used photographers to document events and promote ideology. Photographers included <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Hoffmann_(photographer)" title="Heinrich Hoffmann (photographer)">Heinrich Hoffmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Jaeger" title="Hugo Jaeger">Hugo Jaeger</a>. Hoffmann worked in his father's photographic shop and as a photographer in Munich from 1908. He joined the NSDAP on 6 April 1920. After Hitler took over the party in 1921, he named Hoffmann as his official photographer, a post he held for over a quarter-century. A photograph taken by Hoffmann in Munich's Odeonsplatz on show of 2 August 1914s a young Hitler among the crowds cheering the outbreak of World War I and was used in Nazi propaganda. Hitler and Hoffmann became close friends—in fact, when Hitler became the ruler of Germany, Hoffmann was the only man authorized to take official photographs of him. Hoffmann's photographs were published as postage stamps, postcards, posters and picture books. Following Hoffmann's suggestion, both he and Hitler received royalties from all uses of Hitler's image (even on postage stamps), which made Hoffmann a millionaire. In 1933 he was elected to the Reichstag and in 1938 Hitler appointed him a 'Professor'.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R99057,_%22Wolfsschanze%22,_Adolf_Hitler_mit_Stab.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R99057%2C_%22Wolfsschanze%22%2C_Adolf_Hitler_mit_Stab.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R99057%2C_%22Wolfsschanze%22%2C_Adolf_Hitler_mit_Stab.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R99057%2C_%22Wolfsschanze%22%2C_Adolf_Hitler_mit_Stab.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R99057%2C_%22Wolfsschanze%22%2C_Adolf_Hitler_mit_Stab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R99057%2C_%22Wolfsschanze%22%2C_Adolf_Hitler_mit_Stab.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R99057%2C_%22Wolfsschanze%22%2C_Adolf_Hitler_mit_Stab.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="524" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R99057,_%22Wolfsschanze%22,_Adolf_Hitler_mit_Stab.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hitler's field headquarters, Hitler with staff, May or June 1940, <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Hoffmann_(photographer)" title="Heinrich Hoffmann (photographer)">Heinrich Hoffmann</a> front row far right</div>
</div>
</div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>
